<div id="review_246908258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246908258" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5852865-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533064206p2/5852865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246908258?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/5852865-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246908258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6869980362713554994">When I was a "real" children's librarian, I tried to maintain a familiarity with the books that were popular with kids, which occasionally meant reading books that didn't live up to my lofty literary standards. Since I don't work directly with the public anymore, I rarely take the time to read mediocre books on purpose. Sometimes I feel like this gives me a skewed set of standards for the books I do read. It's easy to nitpick A Monster Calls when you're comparing it to Breadcrumbs, instead of th</span>
  <span id="freeText6869980362713554994" style="display:none">When I was a "real" children's librarian, I tried to maintain a familiarity with the books that were popular with kids, which occasionally meant reading books that didn't live up to my lofty literary standards. Since I don't work directly with the public anymore, I rarely take the time to read mediocre books on purpose. Sometimes I feel like this gives me a skewed set of standards for the books I do read. It's easy to nitpick A Monster Calls when you're comparing it to Breadcrumbs, instead of the latest Monster High (see? I've totally heard of that series). <br /><br />For that reason, it's refreshing to read a book like The Emerald Atlas. The author wrote for Gossip Girl and The OC, and it shows. Two of the protagonists are cardboard cutouts, straight out of the latest High School Musical franchise - the nerdy boy, the small but scrappy girl - and their dialogue is wince-inducing. The eldest child is slightly better developed, but she still only has one guiding motivation. The villains are laughable, prancing around caves and dilapidated castles in mustache-twirling glee. <br /><br />As for the settings... As the book opens, the children are spending time in the Edgar Allan Poe Home for Hopeless and Incorrigible Orphans. If you're going to throw a whopper of a place name like that into your novel, it better have a (hopefully ironic, self-mocking) tone to match. This one doesn't. <br /><br />Now that I've gotten all of that out of the way, though, let me hasten to say that I would totally recommend this book to kids if I were still doing active readers' advisory. The plot is reasonably well-crafted (though I suspect there are probably holes, since it is a time travel tale), the pacing is pretty good, and it's full of monsters and action. The message of family loyalty and forgiveness (not that I support didacticism, mind you) is a positive one too. <br /><br />So, yes. I would send this book home with lots of kids, and they would probably love it. But Breadcrumbs is better. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6869980362713554994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897665398?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64448521-noah-pindak?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64448521-noah-pindak?shelf=time-traveling">time-traveling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64448521-noah-pindak?shelf=witty-yet-emotional">witty-yet-emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64448521-noah-pindak?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897665398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8816233906738755089">4.5 Stars✨<br/><br/>This wonderful series is dear to my bookish heart. I've reread it multiple times since I first discovered it back in 2012, and was immediately obsessed with it before I ever got hooked on Harry Potter. I'm a Ravenclaw btw.😉<br/><br/>It's a spectacular introduction into a compelling world of interesting characters and backstories, where three books have the power of making and unmaking the world. And those mystical and mythic books are called the Books of Beginning. Unquestionably, the three main</span>
  <span id="freeText8816233906738755089" style="display:none">4.5 Stars✨<br /><br />This wonderful series is dear to my bookish heart. I've reread it multiple times since I first discovered it back in 2012, and was immediately obsessed with it before I ever got hooked on Harry Potter. I'm a Ravenclaw btw.😉<br /><br />It's a spectacular introduction into a compelling world of interesting characters and backstories, where three books have the power of making and unmaking the world. And those mystical and mythic books are called the Books of Beginning. Unquestionably, the three main protagonists - Kate, Michael, and Emma - are well written, worth cheering on, and have emotional baggage that is tastefully explored and developed. Each are uniquely different, intelligent, and hilarious. Side note: Emma is my fighter queen, who I adore and send all the positive vibes to. Also I relate more to her as I'm the youngest lol.<br /><br />Time traveling is such a difficult and strange subplot to involve in any piece of fiction, especially fantasy. I love how the aspects of rewriting the past and undoing terrible tragedies are played around with and questioned throughout this marvelous middle grade novel.📗💚<br /><br />Another underlying theme is the power of love, specifically familial love. True love of family and one's own kindred. The depth of which we go to help who we love, how that love can drive us. And how it drives Kate throughout the book. She's a realistic character who grapples with protecting her younger siblings while trying to comprehend her own past, who she is, and what her real destiny is. Kate is just the best.😍<br /><br />Definitely check out this trilogy. It's delightful, thrilling, funny, and surprisingly deep and emotional for a children's series. These characters are compelling and the story kept me turning the pages. It's spectacular.<br /><br />I'd love to know what you think of "The Emerald Atlas!" But in the meantime - remember your worth and happy reading.😗📖</span>
  <a data-text-id="8816233906738755089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Adam Silvera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4050629-adam-silvera"><img alt="Adam Silvera" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595433626p2/4050629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159122211?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Silvera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Silvera" href="/user/show/4050629-adam-silvera">Adam Silvera</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4050629-adam-silvera?shelf=52-youngster-books-for-2011">52-youngster-books-for-2011</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159122211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17409142880507655510">Totally enjoyed this one. The three main characters (Kate, Michael and Emma) are three children who are bouncing from orphanage to orphanage, insisting that they aren't to be called "orphans" because their parents aren't dead and will return to them, They hold onto this ten years later since their departure. <br/><br/>Kate was a great big sis, a remarkably strong character, and Emma was hilariously bold for such a young girl, but Michael was hands-down my favorite character with his belief in the fantasy </span>
  <span id="freeText17409142880507655510" style="display:none">Totally enjoyed this one. The three main characters (Kate, Michael and Emma) are three children who are bouncing from orphanage to orphanage, insisting that they aren't to be called "orphans" because their parents aren't dead and will return to them, They hold onto this ten years later since their departure. <br /><br />Kate was a great big sis, a remarkably strong character, and Emma was hilariously bold for such a young girl, but Michael was hands-down my favorite character with his belief in the fantasy (particularly dwarves) long before discovering the reality of it, which spawned from the sentimental value of a book his father left behind for him. I could probably read a book on a character just like Michael, and have often played at the thought of writing a story on a character much like him. I love Michael's (pretty impressionable) view on elves as well; hilarious. <br /><br />It's a great fantasy book for readers that loved: <br />-Lord of the Rings<br />-Harry Potter<br />-Chronicles of Narnia<br />-A Series of Unfortunate Events <br /><br />...And probably a couple of other classics that are slipping my mind in this late-early hour. It has a bit of everything in it while maintaining original and wouldn't shock me if I'm still hearing about it twenty years from now. <br /><br />OH! Beautiful cover. Amazingly awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17409142880507655510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094806569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13220758873106163783">This is the first entry in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/59037-the-books-of-beginning' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Books of Beginning</a> series by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4766257.John_Stephens' title='John Stephens' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Stephens</a>. The story is very dramatic, with a host of magical creatures and danger at every turn.<br/><br/> The three 'orphans' - Kate, Michael, and Emma - have the same older sister, middle brother, baby sister composition as the books featuring our favorite orphan siblings: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/42069-a-series-of-unfortunate-events' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Series of Unfortunate Events</a>. <br/><br/>The plot can be confusing, as the characters traveling back and forth through time and interacting with the same people, changing history</span>
  <span id="freeText13220758873106163783" style="display:none">This is the first entry in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/59037-the-books-of-beginning" rel="nofollow noopener">The Books of Beginning</a> series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4766257.John_Stephens" title="John Stephens" rel="nofollow noopener">John Stephens</a>. The story is very dramatic, with a host of magical creatures and danger at every turn.<br /><br /> The three 'orphans' - Kate, Michael, and Emma - have the same older sister, middle brother, baby sister composition as the books featuring our favorite orphan siblings: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/42069-a-series-of-unfortunate-events" rel="nofollow noopener">A Series of Unfortunate Events</a>. <br /><br />The plot can be confusing, as the characters traveling back and forth through time and interacting with the same people, changing history along the way. <br /><br />I really enjoyed listening to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5446186.Jim_Dale" title="Jim Dale" rel="nofollow noopener">Jim Dale</a> narrate the tale aloud on audiobook and I'm looking forward to reading the next book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262797.The_Fire_Chronicle__The_Books_of_Beginning___2_" title="The Fire Chronicle (The Books of Beginning, #2) by John Stephens" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fire Chronicle</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13220758873106163783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BxoGAFoW8UL2zjo+BJcwt0pYWhOCODWT9yg20tl0al9NqOQeg5IPkJ88Ja5jqVZz5u65p+bXy9KFBhgjEK05JA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vC2FmB1BPWqoLBIN6cZwjOY2SpXdNGWC29gTTPXek5L2n2eGxMXDuMHeDZ2O+BZISoCpIbnbm8Op9j29PAfA6Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
